  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_6b7293c5-2a65-41bf-bc49-2c948e85ebaa'
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer2506009108072097216"><b>"You've eaten too much, you fat pig."</b><br/><b></b><br/>When Jessica was thirteen years old, she met the Monkey.<br/><br/>The Monkey lived inside her: a driving, fiery voice telling her that thinness was the only way.   <span id="freeText2506009108072097216" style="display:none"><b>"You've eaten too much, you fat pig."</b><br /><b></b><br />When Jessica was thirteen years old, she met the Monkey.<br /><br />The Monkey lived inside her: a driving, fiery voice telling her that thinness was the only way. The only way to be safe, to be good, to be acceptable and above all, to escape from the cold, looming threat of approaching adulthood. Jessica listened to the Monkey, and it consumed her.<br /><br />This is the illuminating story of a teenage girl's wanderings in darkness: the spiral down into madness, the terrible realities of an adolescent psychiatric unit, and the stark choice that she must either tame her monster - or die.<br /><br />Through memory, reflection, and enduring black humour, Jessica makes a tenuous peace with the world and with her emerging adult self.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12579279262614114547">I first heard of Monkey Taming through a recommendation from my friend, and from the moment I started reading, I was automatically hooked. This book is mildly graphic (nothing major or traumatizing) since the author is referring to anorexia, so it's more appropriate for teenagers. I enjoyed this book a lot! It was very moving; at some points I felt as though I was about to cry. However, that didn't stop my from reading the book in a day. It really is remarkable how the author managed to fully re</span>
  <span id="freeText12579279262614114547" style="display:none">I first heard of Monkey Taming through a recommendation from my friend, and from the moment I started reading, I was automatically hooked. This book is mildly graphic (nothing major or traumatizing) since the author is referring to anorexia, so it's more appropriate for teenagers. I enjoyed this book a lot! It was very moving; at some points I felt as though I was about to cry. However, that didn't stop my from reading the book in a day. It really is remarkable how the author managed to fully recover from such a disease and it's very creative of her to retell her story through the protagonist Jessica. I recommend this book to anyone who lives for tales of the powerful and meaningful catagory; especially to those that have had experiences with eating disorders. Anorexia Nervosa in particular.</span>

<div id="review_648811056" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/648811056" />
    <a title="Bridget" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17322561-bridget"><img alt="Bridget" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481879314p2/17322561.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/648811056?book_show_action=true">Jun 23, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bridget" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bridget" href="/user/show/17322561-bridget">Bridget</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer648811056&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer648811056" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5193407603273473331">I initially read this book ten years ago when I found it at my local library and I was in the grips of an eating disorder. It gave me so much comfort to know I wasn’t alone and to start to feel like maybe recovery was a possibility. I loved the book a lot and could relate to many of the characters who were struggling in the book.<br/><br/>I decided to reread it again recently, now that I’ve been fully recovered for a number of years. I fell in love with it again. Yes it brought up so many somewhat painful</span>
  <span id="freeText5193407603273473331" style="display:none">I initially read this book ten years ago when I found it at my local library and I was in the grips of an eating disorder. It gave me so much comfort to know I wasn’t alone and to start to feel like maybe recovery was a possibility. I loved the book a lot and could relate to many of the characters who were struggling in the book.<br /><br />I decided to reread it again recently, now that I’ve been fully recovered for a number of years. I fell in love with it again. Yes it brought up so many somewhat painful memories, but it also brought me so much relief to remember that I got out. <br /><br />The only reasons I’ve given it 4 stars instead of 5 is because I know my past self would have taken all the weights, heights and calories in the book and then compared them to myself. So although I don’t remember being triggered when I read it many years ago, I do know it can be a huge trigger for those living with eating disorders to see numbers and then feel not sick enough. And I believe like the writer could have still had the same impact with her novel without including the numbers. <br />My second reason for giving it 4 stars is that her recovery suddenly happened, it became rushed in the final few pages and she was suddenly better. I think I would have liked more detail into her recovery as things started to improve. <br /><br />Apart from that, I had also forgotten the author had a lived experience of anorexia, so reading that at the end made me cry a bit. Only because I was so happy she managed to recover.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5193407603273473331" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2465361202" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2465361202" />
    <a title="Jodie Louise  WitchinnReadin &amp;#x1f525;" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5885985-jodie-louise-witchinnreadin-x1f525"><img alt="Jodie Louise  WitchinnReadin &amp;#x1f525;" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1496997766p2/5885985.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2465361202?book_show_action=true">Aug 28, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jodie Louise  WitchinnReadin &amp;#x1f525;" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jodie Louise  WitchinnReadin &amp;#x1f525;" href="/user/show/5885985-jodie-louise-witchinnreadin-x1f525">Jodie Louise  WitchinnReadin &amp;#x1f525;</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2465361202" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6144027850660817045"><b>Trigger Warnings: Eating disorders, self harm, suicidal thoughts & depression. <br/><i>I'm going to hide this review for the minor spoilers and just in case someone may find it potentially triggering</i></b><br/><br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[Annorexia Nervosa has the highest mortality rate of any other mental illness, it has been found that without treatment twenty percent of people who suffer from eating disorders die. People with anorexia feel a compulsive need to lose weight and have a crippling fear of gaining weight. It effec</span></span>
  <span id="freeText6144027850660817045" style="display:none"><b>Trigger Warnings: Eating disorders, self harm, suicidal thoughts &amp; depression. <br /><i>I'm going to hide this review for the minor spoilers and just in case someone may find it potentially triggering</i></b><br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Annorexia Nervosa has the highest mortality rate of any other mental illness, it has been found that without treatment twenty percent of people who suffer from eating disorders die. People with anorexia feel a compulsive need to lose weight and have a crippling fear of gaining weight. It effects every aspect of their life and there are many factors in eating disorders that effect each person that suffers differently and i feel that Judith Fathallah perfectly shows the struggles and severity of this illness in Monkey Taming- You've eaten too much you fat pig. <br /><br />Jessica Hassan is a thirteen year old, who like women of all ages makes the decision once again to lose weight. She will cut out all pizza, ice-cream and those cursed Dairy-lea triangles that are her comfort blanket. She's made the decision many times before but has never managed to stick to her promises of no more junk food that is until she's on a family holiday and after one too many comments about weight Jessica vows she will lose weight, and she does cutting her food intake drastically and with the extra activities her and her family do whilst on holiday Jessica loses nearly a stone, with that a switch is flicked in Jessica's mind and she falls down the rabbit hole into the obsessions of eating disorders as Jess's weight decreases her obsession increases. <br /><br />Jessica's mental voice is mature for a thirteen year old, she's an intelligent child who after suffering a crippling loss and other family dramas finds the control she didn't have in other aspects of her life in her strict daily routine all in the name of weight loss. We see through out the story the further and further she gets into her illness the more it effects her friendships, family life, her daily routine and her moods turning Jess into someone her friends and family no longer feel like they know. <br /><br />Some Anorexic's have a mental voice that constantly berates them and makes them believe that thinness is the way to happiness, the way to perfection. Jess calls hers the Monkey, the Monkey is always there in Jess's mind controlling her fighting with Jess's inner voice as slowly it consumes her and drags her down into her illness. <br /><br />Through out the story we see Jess's full spiral into Anorexia, how it starts wanting to lose a few pounds thinking as many people do, everything will be better when i'm skinny, into the compulsions of under eating, calorie counting and a strict exercise regime. Jess could not leave the house until she had weighed herself and done her exercises correctly- one wrong move and should would have to redo the lot sometimes more than once. Before long Jess is dangerously underweight, her mood are in turmoil and the Monkey's voice is getting louder, stronger and more demanding of Jess everyday. Jess is admitted into an adolescent psychiatric unit where she meets other teens some with eating disorders, some with depression and some who self harm. The unit is not somewhere the Monkey feels Jess should be still pushing her to starve herself whilst people are fighting to help Jess recover. The time Jess is in the unit isn't sugar coated, it's a dark time and harrowing as to just what an struggle it is for people fighting to recover.<br /><br />Monkey Taming is in my opinion an excellent book showing the true damage eating disorders can to to a person's mind, body &amp; soul. This is an incredibly insightful book into the mind of someone suffering with an eating disorder, it is a mildly graphic book but it is a book i would highly recommend someone to read who would not find it to be potentially triggering. I think that Monkey Taming could give insight to someone who knows someone who is suffering from an eating disorder just so they can have some idea as to what they're going through and recovery is not as easy or simple as eating something. <br /><br />I enjoyed everything about this book but i especially enjoyed reading the growth and development of Jess and her Mum's relationship, it really is a fantastic read. I have read a few books on eating disorders but specifically about Anorexia and this is hands down my favourite. I feel even people without an ED can relate slightly in someway, feeling the need to lose weight through peer pressure, or feeling it will make everything better is something many people deal with. <br /><br />I gave this book five stars not just for the story itself which is captivating in itself but because of the insight it could give someone who has someone in their life struggling with an eating disorder. It is a mildly graphic book and could be triggering to some people so please only read this if you feel you are well enough. <br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="6144027850660817045" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1386586948" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1386586948?book_show_action=true">Sep 08, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chiara Duchi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chiara Duchi" href="/user/show/46385600-chiara-duchi">Chiara Duchi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1386586948" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2969312751296054101">This book's absolutely worth reading for everyone, especially for teen girls who want to lose weight because of peer pressure or because they feel they're not enough. I think that everybody can learn a lot from this book, as I did. <br/>Well, I basically ate it because, reading word after word and recognizing myself in every page, gave me an incredible sensation. It made me understand that I wasn't the only girl who suffered that way. I read this book at the age of 14, now I'm 17; this story helped m</span>
  <span id="freeText2969312751296054101" style="display:none">This book's absolutely worth reading for everyone, especially for teen girls who want to lose weight because of peer pressure or because they feel they're not enough. I think that everybody can learn a lot from this book, as I did. <br />Well, I basically ate it because, reading word after word and recognizing myself in every page, gave me an incredible sensation. It made me understand that I wasn't the only girl who suffered that way. I read this book at the age of 14, now I'm 17; this story helped me destroying the wall that I built inside myself so that I felt even better, day after day. I would strongly recommend this book to any teen girl, just to know something about eating disorders such as anorexia and bulimia (which are well explained here) and approach to them. Some people might tell me that it's not a good idea to recommend this book to girls who aren't affected by an eating disease. Instead, I believe that it's really important for everyone to realize how you can feel and how terrible it is to "wander in darkness". I think everyone should be told they're beautiful until they believe it. Nowadays, we've become so accostumed to the airbrushed pictures (on the Internet, magazines, TV ecc.) that it's easy to forget what the average woman's body really looks like. We definitely have to change our culture's idea of beauty in order to reduce the number of people affected by anorexia. And then I would say that I've never met a girl I couldn't call a beauty.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2969312751296054101" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Michelle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6367703-michelle"><img alt="Michelle" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/279806098?book_show_action=true">Feb 18, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle" href="/user/show/6367703-michelle">Michelle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6367703-michelle?shelf=february">february</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer279806098" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1952011422083033807"> 'Monkey Taming; You've Eaten too much you Fat Pig', is about a thirteen-year-old girl named Jessica, who's under the pressure to be thin. She deals with comments about her weight everyday, & finally one day she decides she refuses to give the others something to make fun of her about; she will be thin. So, she goes anorexic, only wanting to be accepted & deciding this is the only way, unaware of the dark hell hole she has put herself in. <br/><br/>I finished this book, because I thought it was really, re</span>
  <span id="freeText1952011422083033807" style="display:none"> 'Monkey Taming; You've Eaten too much you Fat Pig', is about a thirteen-year-old girl named Jessica, who's under the pressure to be thin. She deals with comments about her weight everyday, &amp; finally one day she decides she refuses to give the others something to make fun of her about; she will be thin. So, she goes anorexic, only wanting to be accepted &amp; deciding this is the only way, unaware of the dark hell hole she has put herself in. <br /><br />I finished this book, because I thought it was really, really good. It's now one of my favorite books, &amp; I really wanted to find out how Jessica would be able to fight off the 'Monkey', &amp; a disease as bad as anorexia.<br /><br />I picked this book up, because it seemed like a really good read, &amp; the title caught my eye. I like reading about things that happen in real life, &amp; people suffer from anorexia everyday. I felt like this book gave me an insider's opinion on what REALLY goes on in this disease, not how the media glamorizes it.<br /><br />I would recommend this book to ALL girls. Everywhere. No one will ever be completely satisfied with the way they look, &amp; I think this book will make them think twice before making a decision they'd later on regret, or give them that little bit more of spirit to fight the horrible disease.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer6196901275802042892">I have read this book over and over since I bought it in 2007. I would say I have given it a read at least once a year since then - so about 8 or 9 times. <br/><br/>Every time I read it, I am reminded of what a crazy world we live in, and how even though people try to portray that they are perfect, they are still only human, with hopes and dreams, fears and insecurities. <br/><br/>Judith Fathallah has the most tender way of writing about something so ugly - her innocence has been taken, but who she is still exists </span>
  <span id="freeText6196901275802042892" style="display:none">I have read this book over and over since I bought it in 2007. I would say I have given it a read at least once a year since then - so about 8 or 9 times. <br /><br />Every time I read it, I am reminded of what a crazy world we live in, and how even though people try to portray that they are perfect, they are still only human, with hopes and dreams, fears and insecurities. <br /><br />Judith Fathallah has the most tender way of writing about something so ugly - her innocence has been taken, but who she is still exists - her kindness and intellect come though in her writing.<br /><br />I enjoyed that the language that she used was simple and clear, and was the perfect mix of narrative clarity and sarcasm and cynicism. <br /><br />The book shows her intelligence beyond her years, and the struggle that even young people can go through, often being dismissed as going through a "phase".<br /><br />Every page brought with it fear and frustration, fascination and intrigue.<br /><br />I would recommend this book to anyone, especially teenagers who may be going through their own struggles.</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9258288664116431779">I first heard of Monkey Taming through a recommendation from my friend, and from the moment I started reading, I was automatically hooked. This book is mildly graphic (nothing major or traumatizing) since the author is referring to anorexia, so it's more appropriate for teenagers. I enjoyed this book a lot! It was very moving; at some points I felt as though I was about to cry. However, that didn't stop my from reading the book in a day. It really is remarkable how the author managed to fully re</span>
  <span id="freeText9258288664116431779" style="display:none">I first heard of Monkey Taming through a recommendation from my friend, and from the moment I started reading, I was automatically hooked. This book is mildly graphic (nothing major or traumatizing) since the author is referring to anorexia, so it's more appropriate for teenagers. I enjoyed this book a lot! It was very moving; at some points I felt as though I was about to cry. However, that didn't stop my from reading the book in a day. It really is remarkable how the author managed to fully recover from such a disease and it's very creative of her to retell her story through the protagonist Jessica. I recommend this book to anyone who lives for tales of the powerful and meaningful catagory; especially to those that have had experiences with eating disorders. Anorexia Nervosa in particular.</span>

It was really relatable without it being triggering. The only reason i did not give is a full five stars was because I felt that the recovery part was a little unrealistic? The way it was written felt more like she recovered overnight rather than it takes an incredible amount of efforts to really eradicate an eating disorder. However, I do understand that this book is more of how the protagonist</span>
  <span id="freeText10811022122544885378" style="display:none">Loved loved loved this book.<br /><br />As a person suffering from an eating disorder, this book was SO on point. It was really relatable without it being triggering. The only reason i did not give is a full five stars was because I felt that the recovery part was a little unrealistic? The way it was written felt more like she recovered overnight rather than it takes an incredible amount of efforts to really eradicate an eating disorder. However, I do understand that this book is more of how the protagonist spiral down to Anorexia and the she submits to the "Monkey."<br /><br />Great book. Would recommend to people suffering/recovering from ED and people who don't to get a detailed realistic insight on how it is to have an ED (not how the media portrayed it to be)</span>

  <span id="freeText9023615593793679452" style="display:none">This book was really incredible. It allows you to understand how anorexia can occur, what effect it can have and how it can ultimately be beaten. You're given a rare insight into the mind of an anorexic in this book with the author being a former sufferer too. I would definitely recommend this if the topic of ED is of an interest to you, or to be honest, even if you just have an odd relationship with food (which I think is a lot more common nowadays). I'm a massive fan of this book and think it really is under appreciated. </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('pXpjZEvQhlqHVbPvPJus72kWoNd+8qqOTGfbYc9aRZdfxp3LOMgSZsiWVmhLlVq1N1qC502+RtEGkLjwNzLptw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('1Tfjt1AIiMnKe6e7rj6oIRGgBoRdepmaRT+g6F8D658vix0YIxAc9YW4QjzZMF57T+wktG42dcUPyMN5p2tHvw==')})
  }

This is the relentlessly honest, fiercely intelligent story of living with both anorexia and binge-eating disorder, moving past her shame, and learning to tell her secret.\n\nWhen Burton was thirteen, her stable life in suburban Michigan was turned upside down by her parents\' abrupt divorce, and she moved to Colorado with her mother and sister. She seized on this move west as an adventure and an opportunity to reinvent herself from middle-school nerd to popular teenage girl. But she hadn\'t escaped unscathed, and in the fallout from her parents\' breakup, an inherited fixation on thinness went from &quot;peculiarity to pathology.&quot; She entered into a painful cycle of anorexia and binge eating that formed a subterranean layer to her sunny life. She went from success to success--she went to Yale, scored a dream job at a magazine right out of college, and married her college boyfriend. But in college the compulsive eating got worse--she\'d binge, swear it would be the last time, and then, hours later, do it again--and after she graduated she descended into anorexia, her attempt to &quot;quit food.&quot;\n\nBinge eating is more prevalent than anorexia or bulimia, but there is less research and little storytelling to help us understand it.
